      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The origin of the word
       <i>
        Andorra
       </i>
       is unknown, although several hypotheses have been formulated. The oldest derivation of the word
       <i>
        Andorra
       </i>
       is from the Greek historian
       <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">
        Polybius
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Histories_(Polybius)" title="The Histories (Polybius)">
         The Histories
        </a>
       </i>
       III, 35, 1) who describes the
       <i>
        Andosins
       </i>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">
        Iberian
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">
        Pre-Roman tribe
       </a>
       , as historically located in the valleys of Andorra and facing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carthaginian" title="Carthaginian">
        Carthaginian
       </a>
       army in its passage through the Pyrenees during the
       <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">
        Punic Wars
       </a>
       . The word
       <i>
        Andosini
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Andosins
       </i>
       (Ἀνδοσίνους) may derive from the
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       <i>
        handia
       </i>
       whose meaning is "big" or "giant".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diccionari_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Diccionari-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Andorran
       <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">
        toponymy
       </a>
       shows evidence of
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque language
       </a>
       in the area. Another theory suggests that the word
       <i>
        Andorra
       </i>
       may derive from the old word
       <i>
        Anorra
       </i>
       that contains the Basque word
       <i>
        ur
       </i>
       (water).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another theory suggests that
       <i>
        Andorra
       </i>
       may derive from
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">
        Arabic
       </a>
       <i>
        al-durra
       </i>
       , meaning "The forest" (الدرة). When the
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Moors
       </a>
       colonized the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       , the valleys of the Pyrenees were covered by large tracts of forest, and other regions and towns, also administered by Muslims, received this designation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other theories suggest that the term derives from the
       <a href="/wiki/Navarro-Aragonese" title="Navarro-Aragonese">
        Navarro-Aragonese
       </a>
       <i>
        andurrial
       </i>
       , which means "land covered with bushes" or "scrubland".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">
        folk etymology
       </a>
       holds that
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       had named the region as a reference to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biblical" title="Biblical">
        Biblical
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Cannan" title="Cannan">
        Canaanite
       </a>
       valley of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">
         Endor
        </a>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">
         Andor
        </a>
       </i>
       (where the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Midianites" title="Midianites">
        Midianites
       </a>
       had been defeated), a name also bestowed by his heir and son
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_le_Debonnaire" title="Louis le Debonnaire">
        Louis le Debonnaire
       </a>
       after defeating the Moors in the "wild valleys of Hell".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Andorra" title="History of Andorra">
        History of Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">
        Prehistory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/220px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/330px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/440px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Roc de les Bruixes
         </i>
         prehistorical sanctuary located in
         <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">
          Canillo
         </a>
         (detail)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="834" data-file-width="819" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/220px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/330px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/440px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">
          Hannibal
         </a>
         's route (in red) during the
         <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">
          Second Punic War
         </a>
         . The Iberian tribes (in green) fought against the
         <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">
          Carthaginian
         </a>
         army in the Pyrenees.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <i>
        La Balma de la
        <a href="/wiki/La_Margineda" title="La Margineda">
         Margineda
        </a>
       </i>
       found by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeologist" title="Archaeologist">
        archaeologists
       </a>
       at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sant_Julia_de_Loria" title="Sant Julia de Loria">
        Sant Julia de Loria
       </a>
       was the first temporal settlement in 9,500 BC as a passing place between the two sides of the Pyrenees. The seasonal camp was perfectly located for hunting and fishing by the groups of hunter-gatherers from
       <a href="/wiki/Ari%C3%A8ge_(river)" title="Ariège (river)">
        Ariege
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Segre_(river)" title="Segre (river)">
        Segre
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neolithic_Age" title="Neolithic Age">
        Neolithic Age
       </a>
       the group of humans moved to the
       <a href="/wiki/Madriu-Perafita-Claror_Valley" title="Madriu-Perafita-Claror Valley">
        Valley of Madriu
       </a>
       (nowadays Natural Parc located in
       <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">
        Escaldes-Engordany
       </a>
       declared
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">
        UNESCO World Heritage Site
       </a>
       ) as a permanent camp in 6640 BC. The population of the valley grew cereals, raised domestic livestock and developed a commercial trade with people from the
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A8gre_(department)" title="Sègre (department)">
        Segre
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Occitania" title="Occitania">
        Occitania
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other archaeological deposits include the
       <i>
        Tombs of
        <a href="/wiki/Segudet" title="Segudet">
         Segudet
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">
        Ordino
       </a>
       ) and
       <i>
        Feixa del Moro
       </i>
       (Sant Julia de Loria) both dated in 490–4300 BC as an example of the
       <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_culture" title="Urnfield culture">
        Urn culture
       </a>
       in Andorra.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200932,_33-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The model of small settlements begin to evolved as a complex urbanism during the
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">
        Metallurgical
       </a>
       items of iron, ancient coins and relicaries can be found in the
       <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">
        ancient sanctuaries
       </a>
       scattered around the country.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">
        sanctuary
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        Roc de les Bruixes
       </i>
       (Stone of the Witches) is maybe the most important archeological complex of this Age in Andorra, located in the parish of
       <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">
        Canillo
       </a>
       , about the rituals of funerals, ancient scripture and engraved stone
       <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">
        murals
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200934,_35,_38,_39_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200934,_35,_38,_39-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Iberian_and_Roman_Andorra">
        The Iberian and Roman Andorra
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Iberian and Roman Andorra">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The inhabitants of the valleys were traditionally associated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">
        Iberians
       </a>
       and historically located in Andorra as the Iberian tribe
       <i>
        Andosins
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Andosini
       </i>
       (Ἀνδοσίνους) during the 7th and 2nd centuries BC. Influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">
        Aquitanias
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_languages" title="Iberian languages">
        Iberian languages
       </a>
       the locals developed some current toponyms. Early writings and documents relating this group of people goes back to the second century BC by the Greek writer
       <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">
        Polybius
       </a>
       in his
       <i>
        Histories
       </i>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">
        Punic Wars
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200943_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200943-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the most significant remains of this era are the Castle of the
       <i>
        Roc d'Enclar
       </i>
       (part of the early
       <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">
        Marca Hispanica
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        l'Anxiu
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Les_Escaldes" title="Les Escaldes">
        Les Escaldes
       </a>
       and
       <i>
        Roc de L'Oral
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">
        Encamp
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200937,_36-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is known the presence of
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman
       </a>
       influence from the 2nd century BC to the 5th century AD. The places found with more Roman presence are in
       <i>
        Camp Vermell
       </i>
       (Red Field) in Sant Julia de Loria and in some places in Encamp as well as in the
       <i>
        Roc d'Enclar
       </i>
       . People continued trading, mainly with wine and cereals, with the Roman cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Urgellet" title="Urgellet">
        Urgellet
       </a>
       (nowaday
       <a href="/wiki/La_Seu_d%27Urgell" title="La Seu d'Urgell">
        La Seu d'Urgell
       </a>
       ) and all across Segre through the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Roman_roads" title="Roman roads">
         Via Romana
        </a>
        Strata Ceretana
       </i>
       (also known as
       <i>
        Strata Confluetana
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200952,_53_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200952,_53-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200944,_45,_46,_47-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_20-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Visigoths_and_Carolingians:_the_legend_of_Charlemagne">
        The Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="447" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/220px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/330px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/440px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
          Charlemagne
         </a>
         instructing his son
         <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">
          Louis the Pious
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Roman Empire">
        fall of the Roman Empire
       </a>
       Andorra came under the influence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       , not remotely from the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Toledo,_Spain#Visigothic_Toledo" title="History of Toledo, Spain">
        Kingdom of Toledo
       </a>
       , but locally from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Urgell" title="Diocese of Urgell">
        Diocese of Urgell
       </a>
       . The Visigoths remained in the valleys for 200 years, during which time
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Christianity" title="Gothic Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       spread. When the
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        Muslim Empire
       </a>
       and its
       <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">
        conquest
       </a>
       of the Iberian Peninsula replaced the ruling Visigoths, Andorra was sheltered from these invaders by the
       <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">
        Franks
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tradition holds that
       <i>
        Charles the Great
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">
        Charlemagne
       </a>
       ) granted a charter to the Andorran people for contingent of five thousand soldiers under the command of
       <i>
        Marc Almugaver
       </i>
       , in return for fighting against the
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Moors
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Port%C3%A9-Puymorens" title="Porté-Puymorens">
        Porté-Puymorens
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Cerdanya" title="Cerdanya">
        Cerdanya
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="591" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/220px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/330px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/440px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The six old parishes named by their
         <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">
          patron saint
         </a>
         as depicted in the
         <i>
          Acta de Consagració i Dotació de la Catedral de la Seu d'Urgell
         </i>
         (839)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Andorra remained part of the Marca Hispanica of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" title="Frankish Empire">
        Frankish Empire
       </a>
       being part of the territory the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Count_of_Urgell" title="Count of Urgell">
        Count of Urgell
       </a>
       and eventually by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgel" title="Bishop of Urgel">
        bishop
       </a>
       of the Diocese of Urgell. Also tradition holds that it was guaranteed by the son of Charlemagne,
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">
        Louis the Pious
       </a>
       , writing the
       <i>
        Carta de Poblament
       </i>
       or a local
       <a href="/wiki/Municipal_charter" title="Municipal charter">
        municipal charter
       </a>
       circa 805.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 988,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borrell_II" title="Borrell II">
        Borrell II
       </a>
       , Count of Urgell, gave the Andorran valleys to the Diocese of Urgell in exchange for land in Cerdanya.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-histo1_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-histo1-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since then the Bishop of Urgell, based in Seu d'Urgell, has been
       <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">
        Co-prince
       </a>
       of Andorra.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elements_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-elements-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first document that mentions
       <i>
        Andorra
       </i>
       as a territory is the
       <i>
        Acta de Consagració i Dotació de la Catedral de la Seu d'Urgell
       </i>
       (Deed of Consecration and Endowment of the Cathedral of La Seu d'Urgell). The old document dated from 839 depicts the six old
       <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">
        parishes
       </a>
       of the Andorran valleys and therefore the administrative division of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Medieval_Age:_The_Par.C3.A9ages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Age:_The_Paréages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality">
        Medieval Age: The Paréages and the founding of the Co-Principality
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Medieval Age: The Paréages and the founding of the Co-Principality">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1864" data-file-width="2922" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/220px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/330px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/440px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">
          Sant Joan de Caselles
         </a>
         church, dating from the 11th century, part of the Andorran Romanesque heritage
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Before 1095, Andorra did not have any type of military protection and the Bishop of Urgell, who knew that the Count of Urgell wanted to reclaim the Andorran valleys,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elements_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-elements-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       asked the
       <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Caboet" title="Lord of Caboet">
        Lord of Caboet
       </a>
       for help and protection. In 1095 the Lord of Caboet and the Bishop of Urgell signed under oath a declaration of their co-sovereignty over Andorra. Arnalda, daughter of Arnau of Caboet, married the Viscount of Castellbò and both became Viscounts of Castellbò and Cerdanya. Years later their daughter, Ermessenda,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       married
       <a href="/wiki/Roger-Bernard_II,_Count_of_Foix" title="Roger-Bernard II, Count of Foix">
        Roger Bernat II
       </a>
       , the French
       <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Foix" title="Count of Foix">
        Count of Foix
       </a>
       . They became Roger Bernat II and Ermessenda I, Counts of Foix, Viscounts of Castellbò and Cerdanya, and co-sovereigns of Andorra (shared with the Bishop of Urgell).
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 13th century, a military dispute arose between the Bishop of Urgell and the Count of Foix as aftermath of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathar_Crusade" title="Cathar Crusade">
        Cathar Crusade
       </a>
       . The conflict was resolved in 1278 with the mediation of the king of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">
        Aragon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pere_el_Gran" title="Pere el Gran">
        Pere II
       </a>
       between the Bishop and the Count, by the signing of the
       <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A9age_of_Andorra_1278" title="Paréage of Andorra 1278">
        first paréage
       </a>
       which provided that Andorra's sovereignty be shared between the count of Foix
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elements_31-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-elements-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (whose title would ultimately transfer to the French head of state) and the Bishop of Urgell, in
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       . This gave the
       <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">
        principality
       </a>
       its territory and political form.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="714" data-file-width="1092" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Monument commemorating in 1978 the 700th anniversary of the Paréages, located outside
         <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">
          Casa de la Vall
         </a>
         in the capital city of
         <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
          Andorra la Vella
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/220px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/330px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/440px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apse fresco of
         <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters">
          Sant Miquel d'Engolasters
         </a>
         church, painted by
         <i>
          Mestre de Santa Coloma
         </i>
         during the 12th century
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
          <a href="#cite_note-36">
           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A second paréage was signed in 1288 after a dispute when the
       <a href="/wiki/Roger-Bernard_III,_Count_of_Foix" title="Roger-Bernard III, Count of Foix">
        Count of Foix
       </a>
       ordered the construction of a castle in
       <i>
        Roc d'Enclar
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_34-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas2013-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The document was ratified by the noble notary
       <a href="/wiki/County_of_Cerdanya" title="County of Cerdanya">
        Jaume Orig of Puigcerdà
       </a>
       and the construction of military structures in the country was prohibited.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_32-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1364 the political organization of the country named the figure of the
       <a href="/wiki/Syndic" title="Syndic">
        syndic
       </a>
       (now spokesman and president of the parliament) as representative of the Andorrans to their co-princes making possible the creation of
       <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">
        local departments
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        comuns
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        quarts
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        veïnats
       </i>
       ). After being ratified by the Bishop Francesc Tovia and the Count
       <a href="/wiki/John_I,_Count_of_Foix" title="John I, Count of Foix">
        Jean I
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        Consell de la Terra
       </i>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/General_Council_(Andorra)" title="General Council (Andorra)">
        Consell General de les Valls
       </a>
       (General Council of the Valleys) was founded in 1419, the second oldest parliament in Europe. The syndic Andreu d'Alàs and the General Council organized the creation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra#Judicial_branch" title="Politics of Andorra">
        Justice Courts
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        La Cort de Justicia
       </i>
       ) in 1433 with the Co-Princes and the collection of taxes like
       <i>
        foc i lloc
       </i>
       (literally
       <i>
        fire and site
       </i>
       , a national tax active since then).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although we can find remains of ecclesiastical works dating before the 9th century (
       <i>
        Sant Vicenç d'Enclar
       </i>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Santa_Coloma" title="Església de Santa Coloma">
        Església de Santa Coloma
       </a>
       ), Andorra developed exquisite
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanesque_Art_and_Architecture" title="Romanesque Art and Architecture">
        Romanesque Art
       </a>
       during the 9th through 14th centuries, as much in the construction of churches, bridges, religious murals and statues of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_and_Child" title="Virgin and Child">
        Virgin and Child
       </a>
       (being the most important the
       <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">
        Our Lady of Meritxell
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nowadays, the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_regional_characteristics_of_Romanesque_churches#Romanesque_churches_in_Spain.2C_Portugal_and_Andorra" title="List of regional characteristics of Romanesque churches">
        Romanesque
       </a>
       buildings that form part of
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage_of_Andorra" title="Cultural Heritage of Andorra">
        Andorra's cultural heritage
       </a>
       stand out in a remarkable way, with an emphasis on
       <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Esteve" title="Església de Sant Esteve">
        Església de Sant Esteve
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">
        Sant Joan de Caselles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters">
        Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sant_Mart%C3%AD_de_la_Cortinada" title="Sant Martí de la Cortinada">
        Sant Martí de la Cortinada
       </a>
       and the medieval bridges of
       <a href="/wiki/Pont_de_la_Margineda" title="Pont de la Margineda">
        Margineda
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">
        Escalls
       </a>
       among many others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200948,_49,_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200948,_49,-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarcia2011_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarcia2011-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While the Catalan Pyrenees were embryonic of the
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan language
       </a>
       at the end of the 11th century Andorra was influenced by the appearance of that language where it was adopted by proximity and influence even decades before it was expanded by the rest of the Kingdom of Aragon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The local population based its economy during the Middle Ages in the livestock and agriculture, as well as in furs and weavers. Later, at the end of the 11th century, the first
       <a href="/wiki/Bloomery#Medieval_Europe" title="Bloomery">
        foundries of iron
       </a>
       began to appear in Northern Parishes like
       <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">
        Ordino
       </a>
       , much appreciated by the master artisans who developed the art of the forges, an important economic activity in the country from the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_27-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnne_Doustaly-Dunyach2011_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnne_Doustaly-Dunyach2011-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">
        16th to 18th centuries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="400" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/220px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/330px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Main hall of
         <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra">
          <i>
           Tribunal de Corts
          </i>
         </a>
         (High Court of Justice) inside
         <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">
          Casa de la Vall
         </a>
         , the central Judiciary Court of Andorra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1601 the
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra">
        Tribunal de Corts
       </a>
       (High Court of Justice) was created as a result of
       <a href="/wiki/Huguenot_rebellions" title="Huguenot rebellions">
        Huguenot rebellions
       </a>
       from France,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Inquisition
       </a>
       courts coming from Spain and
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_mythology_about_witches" title="Catalan mythology about witches">
        indigenous witchcraft
       </a>
       experienced in the country due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">
        Reformation
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
        Counter-Reformation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the passage of time, the co-title to Andorra passed to the kings of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">
        Navarre
       </a>
       . After Henry of Navarre became King
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">
        Henry IV of France
       </a>
       , he issued an edict in 1607, that established the head of the French state and the Bishop of Urgell as
       <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">
        Co-Princes of Andorra
       </a>
       . During 1617 communal councils form the
       <i>
        sometent
       </i>
       (popular militia or army) to deal with the rise of
       <i>
        bandolerisme
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Brigandage" title="Brigandage">
        brigandage
       </a>
       ) and the Consell de la Terra was defined and structured in terms of its composition, organization and competences current today .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50_44-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas201342_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordi_Planellas201342-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199853,_54,_56_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199853,_54,_56-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Andorra continues with the same economic system that it had during the 12th-14th centuries with a large production of metallurgy (
       <i>
        fargues
       </i>
       , a system similar to
       <i>
        Farga catalana
       </i>
       ) and with the introduction of
       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">
        tobacco
       </a>
       circa 1692 and import trade. The
       <a href="/wiki/Fair" title="Fair">
        fair
       </a>
       of Andorra la Vella was ratified by the co-princes in 1371 and 1448 being the most important annual national festival commercially ever since.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3423" data-file-width="5135" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/220px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/330px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/440px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">
          Manor house
         </a>
         of Rossell family in
         <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">
          Ordino
         </a>
         ,
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">
           Casa Rossell
          </a>
         </i>
         , built in 1611. The family owned in 1619 also the largest ironwork forges in Andorra as
         <i>
          Farga Rossell
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          Farga del Serrat
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
          <a href="#cite_note-52">
           [52]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The country had a unique and experienced
       <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">
        guild
       </a>
       of weavers,
       <i>
        Confraria de Paraires i Teixidors
       </i>
       , located in
       <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">
        Escaldes-Engordany
       </a>
       founded in 1604 taking advantage of the thermal waters of the area. By the time the country constitutes the social system of
       <i>
        prohoms
       </i>
       (wealthy society) and
       <i>
        casalers
       </i>
       (rest of the population with smaller economic acquisition), deriving to the tradition of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pubilla" title="Pubilla">
         pubilla
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heir" title="Heir">
        <i>
         hereu
        </i>
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni2009106,_107_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni2009106,_107-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Three centuries after its foundation the Consell de la Terra locates its headquarters and the Tribunal de Corts in
       <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">
        Casa de la Vall
       </a>
       in 1702. The
       <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">
        manor house
       </a>
       built in 1580 served as a noble fortress of the Busquets family. Inside the parliament was placed the
       <i>
        Closet of the six keys
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Armari de les sis claus
       </i>
       ) representative of each Andorran parish and where the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andorran_constitution" title="Andorran constitution">
        Andorran constitution
       </a>
       and other documents and laws were kept later on.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200982_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Antoni200982-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In both
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerra_dels_Segadors" title="Guerra dels Segadors">
        Guerra dels Segadors
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerra_de_Sucesi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Guerra de Sucesión Española">
        Guerra de Sucesión Española
       </a>
       conflicts, the Andorran people (although with the statement neutral country) supported the
       <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">
        Catalans
       </a>
       who saw their
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_constitutions" title="Catalan constitutions">
        rights
       </a>
       reduced in
       <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">
        1716
       </a>
       . The reaction was the promotion of Catalan writings in Andorra, with cultural works such as the
       <i>
        Book of Privileges
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Llibre de Privilegis de 1674
       </i>
       ),
       <i>
        Manual Digest
       </i>
       (1748) by Antoni Fiter i Rossell or the
       <i>
        Polità andorrà
       </i>
       (1763) by Antoni Puig.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_59-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century:_the_New_Reform_and_the_Andorran_Question">
        19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="461" data-file-width="361" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png/220px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png/330px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/76/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Portrait of
         <a href="/wiki/Casa_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Casa d'Areny-Plandolit">
          Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit
         </a>
         , nobleman and politician who promoted the
         <i>
          New Reform
         </i>
         in 1866
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the French Revolution, in 1809, Napoleon I reestablished the Co-Principate and deleted the French medieval tithe. However, in 1812–13, the
       <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">
        First French Empire
       </a>
       annexed Catalonia during the
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        Peninsular War
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Guerra del francés
       </i>
       ). They divided it into four
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" title="Département">
        départements
       </a>
       , with Andorra being made part of the district of
       <a href="/wiki/Puigcerd%C3%A0" title="Puigcerdà">
        Puigcerdà
       </a>
       (département of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A8gre" title="Sègre">
        Sègre
       </a>
       ). In 1814 a royal decree reestablished the independence and economy of Andorra.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342,_343_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342,_343-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During this period, Andorra's late medieval institutions and rural culture remained largely unchanged. In 1866 the syndic
       <a href="/wiki/Casa_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Casa d'Areny-Plandolit">
        Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit
       </a>
       led the
       <i>
        reformist
       </i>
       group in a Council General of 24 members, elected by suffrage limited to heads of families, replaced the aristocratic oligarchy that previously ruled the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The New Reform (
       <i>
        Nova Reforma
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Pla de Reforma
       </i>
       ) began after being ratified by both Co-Princes and established the basis of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">
        constitution
       </a>
       and symbols (such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Andorra" title="Flag of Andorra">
        tricolor flag
       </a>
       ) of Andorra. A new
       <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">
        service economy
       </a>
       arose as a demand of the inhabitants of the valleys and began to build infrastructures such as hotels, spa resorts, roads and telegraph lines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192,_193_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192,_193-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191,_192,_193_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191,_192,_193-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345_a_347_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345_a_347-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegalàs201293_a_95_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegalàs201293_a_95-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="263" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg/220px-Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Illustration of a scene from the streets of
         <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">
          Canillo
         </a>
         during the
         <i>
          Revolution of 1881
         </i>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
          <a href="#cite_note-69">
           [69]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The authorities of the Co-Princes (
       <i>
        veguer
       </i>
       ) banned casinos and betting houses throughout the country by establishing an economic conflict with the demand of the Andorran people. The conflict led to the so-called
       <i>
        Revolution of 1881
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Troubles of Andorra
       </i>
       , when revolutionaries assaulted the house of the syndic during 8 December 1880 and established the
       <i>
        Provisional Revolutionary Council
       </i>
       led by Joan Pla i Calvo and Pere Baró i Mas, who granted the construction of casinos and spas to foreign companies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198,_199,_203_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198,_199,_203-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During 7 and 9 June 1881, the loyalists of
       <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">
        Canillo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">
        Encamp
       </a>
       reconquered the parishes of
       <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">
        Ordino
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Massana" title="Massana">
        Massana
       </a>
       by establishing contact with the revolutionary forces in
       <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">
        Escaldes-Engordany
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859,_60,_63_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859,_60,_63-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After a day of combat finally the
       <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">
        Treaty of the Bridge of Escalls
       </a>
       was signed the 10 of June.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199658,_59,_60,_61,_62,_63,_64,_65_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199658,_59,_60,_61,_62,_63,_64,_65-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194,_195_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194,_195-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009194,_195_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009194,_195-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348_a_350_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348_a_350-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegalàs201295_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegalàs201295-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Council was replaced and new elections were held. But the economic situation worsened, as society was divided over the
       <i>
        Qüestió d'Andorra
       </i>
       (the
       <i>
        Andorran Question
       </i>
       in relation to the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">
        Eastern Question
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864,_65,_66,_67,_68_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864,_65,_66,_67,_68-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The struggles continued between pro-bishops, pro-French and nationalists who derived the troubles of Canillo in 1882 and 1885.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199667_a_70_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199667_a_70-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198,_199,_202,_203_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198,_199,_202,_203-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352,_353_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352,_353-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Andorra participated in the cultural movement of the Catalan
       <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">
        Renaixença
       </a>
       . Between 1882 and 1887 the first academic schools were formed where trilingualism coexists with the knowledge of the official language, Catalan. Some
       <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">
        romantic
       </a>
       authors from both France and Spain reported the awakening of the
       <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">
        national consciousness
       </a>
       of the country.
       <a href="/wiki/Jacint_Verdaguer" title="Jacint Verdaguer">
        Jacint Verdaguer
       </a>
       lived in Ordino during the 1880s where he wrote and share works related to the Renaixença with
       <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">
        Joaquim de Riba
       </a>
       , writer and photographer.
       <a href="/wiki/Fromental_Hal%C3%A9vy" title="Fromental Halévy">
        Fromental Halévy
       </a>
       , for his part, had already premiered in 1848 the opera
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Le_val_d%27Andorre" title="Le val d'Andorre">
         Le Val d'Andorre
        </a>
       </i>
       of great success in Europe, where the national consciousness of the valleys during the
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">
        Peninsular War
       </a>
       was exposed in the romantic work.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878,_79,_80,_81_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878,_79,_80,_81-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199674_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199674-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354,_355,_356,_357_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354,_355,_356,_357-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEÀrea_de_Recerca_Històrica_del_Govern_d'Andorra200633_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEÀrea_de_Recerca_Històrica_del_Govern_d'Andorra200633-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESegalàs2012_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESegalàs2012-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century:_Modernization_of_the_country_and_the_Constitutional_Andorra">
        20th century: Modernization of the country and the Constitutional Andorra
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 20th century: Modernization of the country and the Constitutional Andorra">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="458" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/180px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/270px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg/360px-Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bor%C3%ADs_Sk%C3%B3syrev.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">
          Boris Skossyreff
         </a>
         , briefly self-proclaimed "King of Andorra" in 1934
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Andorra declared war on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" title="Imperial Germany">
        Imperial Germany
       </a>
       during World War I, but did not take part directly in the fighting. It is known that some Andorrans volunteered to take part in the conflict as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Marching_Regiment_of_the_Foreign_Legion" title="Marching Regiment of the Foreign Legion">
        French Legions
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It remained in an official state of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belligerency" title="Belligerency">
        belligerency
       </a>
       until 1958 as it was not included in the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">
        Treaty of Versailles
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DYKAndorra_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-DYKAndorra-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1933, France occupied Andorra following social unrest which occurred before elections due the
       <i>
        Revolution of 1933
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        FHASA strikes
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Vagues de FHASA
       </i>
       ); the revolt led by
       <i>
        Joves Andorrans
       </i>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">
        labour union group
       </a>
       related to the Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederación Nacional del Trabajo">
        CNT
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_Anarquista_Ib%C3%A9rica" title="Federación Anarquista Ibérica">
        FAI
       </a>
       ) called for political reforms
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">
        universal suffrage vote
       </a>
       of all Andorrans and acted in defense of the rights of local and foreign workers during the construction of FHASA's hydroelectric power station in
       <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">
        Encamp
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 5th April 1933
       <i>
        Joves Andorrans
       </i>
       took the Andorran Parlamient under their custody in rebellion to their requests.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These actions were preceded by the arrival of Colonel René-Jules Baulard with 50
       <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">
        gendarmes
       </a>
       and the mobilization of 200 local militias or
       <i>
        sometent
       </i>
       led by the Síndic Francesc Cairat.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 12 July 1934, adventurer
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">
        Boris Skossyreff
       </a>
       issued a proclamation in Urgell, declaring himself "Boris I, King of Andorra", simultaneously declaring war on the Bishop of Urgell. He was arrested by the Spanish authorities on 20 July and ultimately expelled from
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . From 1936 until 1940, a French military detachment was garrisoned in Andorra to secure the principality against disruption from the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">
        Spanish Civil War
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">
        Francoist Spain
       </a>
       . Francoist troops reached the Andorran border in the later stages of the war. During World War II, Andorra remained neutral and was an important smuggling route between
       <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">
        Vichy France
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Given its relative isolation, Andorra has existed outside the mainstream of European history, with few ties to countries other than
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       . In recent times, however, its thriving tourist industry along with developments in transport and communications have removed the country from its isolation. Its political system was modernized in 1993 after the
       <a href="/wiki/Andorran_constitutional_referendum,_1993" title="Andorran constitutional referendum, 1993">
        Andorran constitutional referendum
       </a>
       , when the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">
        constitution
       </a>
       was drafted by the Co-Princes and the General Council and approved on 14 March
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NS_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NS-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       by 74.2% of voters, with a 76% turnout.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Andorran_parliamentary_election,_1993" title="Andorran parliamentary election, 1993">
        first elections
       </a>
       under the new constitution were held later in the year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NS_92-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NS-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The same year Andorra became a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra" title="Politics of Andorra">
        Politics of Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-princes of Andorra">
        Co-princes of Andorra
       </a>
      </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:290px;max-width:290px">

          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <b>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joan_Enric_Vives_i_Sic%C3%ADlia" title="Joan Enric Vives i Sicília">
            Joan Enric Vives i Sicília
           </a>
          </b>
          <br/>
          –  current
          <a href="/wiki/List_of_Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="List of Co-Princes of Andorra">
           episcopal Co-Prince of Andorra
          </a>
          since 12 May 2003
         </div>
        </div>

         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emmanuel_Macron_in_Tallinn_Digital_Summit._Welcome_dinner_hosted_by_HE_Donald_Tusk._Handshake_(36669381364)_(cropped_2).jpg">
