      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">
        Schools
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Schools">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Children between the ages of 6 and 16 are required by law to have full-time education. Education up to secondary level is provided free of charge by the government.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are three systems of school—Andorran, French, and Spanish—which use Catalan, French, and Spanish, respectively, as the main language of instruction. Parents may choose which system their children attend. All schools are built and maintained by Andorran authorities, but teachers in the French and Spanish schools are paid for the most part by
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . About 50% of Andorran children attend the French primary schools, and the rest attend Spanish or Andorran schools.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Andorra">
        University of Andorra
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: University of Andorra">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Universitat_d%27Andorra" title="Universitat d'Andorra">
        Universitat d'Andorra
       </a>
       (UdA) is the state public university and is the only university in Andorra. It was established in 1997. The university provides first-level degrees in nursing, computer science, business administration, and educational sciences, in addition to higher professional education courses. The only two graduate schools in Andorra are the Nursing School and the School of Computer Science, the latter having a PhD programme.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_Studies_Centre">
        Virtual Studies Centre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Virtual Studies Centre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The geographical complexity of the country as well as the small number of students prevents the University of Andorra from developing a full academic programme, and it serves principally as a centre for virtual studies, connected to Spanish and French universities. The Virtual Studies Centre (
       <i>
        Centre d’Estudis Virtuals
       </i>
       ) at the University runs approximately twenty different academic degrees at both undergraduate and postgraduate levels in fields including tourism, law, Catalan philology, humanities, psychology, political sciences, audiovisual communication, telecommunications engineering, and East Asia studies. The Centre also runs various postgraduate programmes and continuing-education courses for professionals.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">
        Healthcare
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Healthcare">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Healthcare in Andorra is provided to all employed persons and their families by the government-run social security system,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Caixa_Andorrana_de_Seguretat_Social&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Caixa Andorrana de Seguretat Social (page does not exist)">
         Caixa Andorrana de Seguretat Social
        </a>
       </i>
       (CASS), which is funded by employer and employee contributions in respect of salaries. The cost of healthcare is covered by CASS at rates of 75% for out-patient expenses such as medicines and hospital visits, 90% for hospitalisation, and 100% for work-related accidents. The remainder of the costs may be covered by private health insurance. Other residents and tourists require full private health insurance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-travenand_133-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-travenand-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main hospital, Meritxell, is in
       <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">
        Escaldes-Engordany
       </a>
       . There are also 12 primary health care centres in various locations around the principality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cassps_134-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cassps-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Andorra" title="Transport in Andorra">
        Transport in Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport">
        Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="3000" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/220px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/330px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/440px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A train at
         <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">
          Latour-de-Carol
         </a>
         (
         <i>
          La Tor de Querol
         </i>
         ), one of the two stations serving Andorra. Andorra has no railways, although the line connecting Latour-de-Carol and
         <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">
          Toulouse
         </a>
         , which in turn connects to France's
         <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">
          TGVs
         </a>
         at Toulouse, runs within two kilometres (1.2 miles) of the Andorran border.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Until the 20th century, Andorra had very limited transport links to the outside world, and development of the country was affected by its physical isolation. Even now, the nearest major airports at Toulouse and Barcelona are both three hours' drive from Andorra.
      </p>
      <p>
       Andorra has a road network of 279 km (173 mi), of which 76 km (47 mi) is unpaved. The two main roads out of
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
        Andorra la Vella
       </a>
       are the CG-1 to the Spanish border, and the CG-2 to the French border via the Envalira Tunnel near
       <a href="/wiki/El_Pas_de_la_Casa" title="El Pas de la Casa">
        El Pas de la Casa
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mobi_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mobi-135">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Bus services cover all metropolitan areas and many rural communities, with services on most major routes running half-hourly or more frequently during peak travel times. There are frequent long-distance bus services from Andorra to
       <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
        Barcelona
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">
        Toulouse
       </a>
       , plus a daily tour from the former city. Bus services are mostly run by private companies, but some local ones are operated by the government.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are no airports for fixed-wing aircraft within Andorra's borders but there are, however, heliports in
       <a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">
        La Massana
       </a>
       (Camí Heliport),
       <a href="/wiki/Arinsal" title="Arinsal">
        Arinsal
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">
        Escaldes-Engordany
       </a>
       with commercial helicopter services
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heliand_136-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-heliand-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-helitrans_137-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-helitrans-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and an airport located in the neighbouring Spanish comarca of
       <a href="/wiki/Alt_Urgell" title="Alt Urgell">
        Alt Urgell
       </a>
       , 12 kilometres (7.5 miles) south of the Andorran-Spanish border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since July 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport">
        Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport
       </a>
       has operated commercial flights to
       <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport" title="Adolfo Suárez Madrid–Barajas Airport">
        Madrid
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">
        Palma de Mallorca
       </a>
       , and is the
       <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">
        main hub
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Air_Andorra" title="Air Andorra">
        Air Andorra
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Airlines" title="Andorra Airlines">
        Andorra Airlines
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Nearby airports located in
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       provide access to international flights for the principality. The nearest airports are at
       <a href="/wiki/Perpignan%E2%80%93Rivesaltes_Airport" title="Perpignan–Rivesaltes Airport">
        Perpignan
       </a>
       , France (156 kilometres or 97 miles from Andorra) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lleida-Alguaire_Airport" title="Lleida-Alguaire Airport">
        Lleida
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       (160 kilometres or 99 miles from Andorra). The largest nearby airports are at
       <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">
        Toulouse
       </a>
       , France (165 kilometres or 103 miles from Andorra) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barcelona_Airport" title="Barcelona Airport">
        Barcelona
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       (215 kilometres or 134 miles from Andorra). There are hourly bus services from both Barcelona and Toulouse airports to Andorra.
      </p>
      <p>
       The nearest railway station is
       <a href="/wiki/L%27Hospitalet-pr%C3%A8s-l%27Andorre" title="L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre">
        L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre
       </a>
       10 km (6 mi) east of Andorra which is on the
       <span class="nowrap">
        1,435 mm
       </span>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        4 ft
        <span class="frac">
         8
         <span class="visualhide">
         </span>
         <sup>
          1
         </sup>
         ⁄
         <sub>
          2
         </sub>
        </span>
        in
       </span>
       )
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" title="Standard gauge">
        -gauge
       </a>
       line from
       <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">
        Latour-de-Carol
       </a>
       (25 km or 16 mi) southeast of Andorra, to
       <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">
        Toulouse
       </a>
       and on to Paris by the French
       <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">
        high-speed trains
       </a>
       . This line is operated by the
       <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">
        SNCF
       </a>
       . Latour-de-Carol has a scenic
       <span class="nowrap">
        1,000 mm
       </span>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        3 ft
        <span class="frac">
         3
         <span class="visualhide">
         </span>
         <sup>
          3
         </sup>
         ⁄
         <sub>
          8
         </sub>
        </span>
        in
       </span>
       )
       <span class="nowrap">
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metre_gauge" title="Metre gauge">
         metre gauge
        </a>
       </span>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yellow_Train" title="Yellow Train">
        trainline
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Villefranche-de-Conflent" title="Villefranche-de-Conflent">
        Villefranche-de-Conflent
       </a>
       , as well as the SNCF's
       <span class="nowrap">
        1,435 mm
       </span>
       gauge line connecting to
       <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">
        Perpignan
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RENFE" title="RENFE">
        RENFE's
       </a>
       <span class="nowrap">
        1,668 mm
       </span>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        5 ft
        <span class="frac">
         5
         <span class="visualhide">
         </span>
         <sup>
          21
         </sup>
         ⁄
         <sub>
          32
         </sub>
        </span>
        in
       </span>
       )
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberian_gauge" title="Iberian gauge">
        -gauge
       </a>
       line to
       <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
        Barcelona
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also direct
       <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s#Night_trains" title="Intercités">
        Intercités de Nuit
       </a>
       trains between L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre and Paris on certain dates.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_telecommunications">
        Media and telecommunications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media and telecommunications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Andorra" title="Telecommunications in Andorra">
        Telecommunications in Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">
        Andorra Telecom
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Ambox current red.svg" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="360" height="34" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" width="42"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section needs to be
          <b>
           updated
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (November 2015)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In Andorra, mobile and fixed telephone and internet services are operated exclusively by the Andorran national telecommunications company, SOM, also known as
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">
        Andorra Telecom
       </a>
       (STA). The same company also manages the technical infrastructure for national broadcasting of digital television and radio.
      </p>
      <p>
       By the end of 2010, it was planned that every home in the country would have fibre-to-the-home for internet access at a minimum speed of 100 Mbit/s,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-somfo_142-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-somfo-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the availability was complete in June 2012.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is only one Andorran television station,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A0dio_i_Televisi%C3%B3_d%27Andorra" title="Ràdio i Televisió d'Andorra">
         Ràdio i Televisió d'Andorra
        </a>
       </i>
       (RTVA).
       <i>
        Radio Nacional d’Andorra
       </i>
       operates two radio stations,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Radio_Andorra" title="Radio Andorra">
         Radio Andorra
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Andorra Música
       </i>
       . There are three national newspapers,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Diari_d%27Andorra" title="Diari d'Andorra">
         Diari d'Andorra
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/El_Peri%C3%B2dic_d%27Andorra" title="El Periòdic d'Andorra">
         El Periòdic d'Andorra
        </a>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Bondia_(newspaper)" title="Bondia (newspaper)">
         Bondia
        </a>
       </i>
       as well as several local newspapers. There is also an
       <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">
        amateur radio
       </a>
       society.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additional TV and radio stations from
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       are available via digital terrestrial television and IPTV.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Andorra" title="Culture of Andorra">
        Culture of Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Andorra" title="Music of Andorra">
        Music of Andorra
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0309.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2144" data-file-width="2848" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/220px-HPIM0309.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/330px-HPIM0309.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/HPIM0309.JPG/440px-HPIM0309.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HPIM0309.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Andorran flag on balcony, Ordino
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The official and historic language is Catalan. Thus the culture is Catalan, with its own specificity.
      </p>
      <p>
       Andorra is home to folk dances like the contrapàs and marratxa, which survive in
       <a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Julià de Lòria">
        Sant Julià de Lòria
       </a>
       especially. Andorran folk music has similarities to the music of its neighbours, but is especially
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Catalonia" title="Music of Catalonia">
        Catalan
       </a>
       in character, especially in the presence of dances such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Sardana" title="Sardana">
        sardana
       </a>
       . Other Andorran folk dances include contrapàs in
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
        Andorra la Vella
       </a>
       and Saint Anne's dance in Escaldes-Engordany. Andorra's national holiday is
       <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">
        Our Lady of Meritxell
       </a>
       Day, 8 September.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       American folk artist
       <a href="/wiki/Malvina_Reynolds" title="Malvina Reynolds">
        Malvina Reynolds
       </a>
       , intrigued by its defence budget of $4.90, wrote a song "Andorra".
       <a href="/wiki/Pete_Seeger" title="Pete Seeger">
        Pete Seeger
       </a>
       added verses, and sang "Andorra" on his 1962 album
       <i>
        The Bitter and the Sweet
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Andorra is famous for the practice of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_Sports" title="Winter Sports">
        Winter Sports
       </a>
       . Popular sports played in Andorra include
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
        rugby union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        basketball
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">
        roller hockey
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">
        roller hockey
       </a>
       Andorra usually plays in
       <a href="/wiki/CERH_European_Roller_Hockey_Championship" title="CERH European Roller Hockey Championship">
        CERH Euro Cup
       </a>
       and in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">
        FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup
       </a>
       . In 2011, Andorra was the host country to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_European_League_Final_Eight" title="2011 European League Final Eight">
        2011 European League Final Eight
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2128" data-file-width="2832" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/220px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/330px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg/440px-Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadi_Comunal_Vella.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Estadi_Comunal_d%27Andorra_la_Vella" title="Estadi Comunal d'Andorra la Vella">
          Estadi Comunal d'Andorra la Vella
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The country is represented in association football by the
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_football_team" title="Andorra national football team">
        Andorra national football team
       </a>
       . However, the team has had little success internationally because of Andorra's small population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fifa-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Football is ruled in Andorra by the
       <a href="/wiki/Andorran_Football_Federation" title="Andorran Football Federation">
        Andorran Football Federation
       </a>
       - founded in 1994, it organizes the national competitions of association football (
       <a href="/wiki/Primera_Divisi%C3%B3" title="Primera Divisió">
        Primera Divisió
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Copa_Constituci%C3%B3" title="Copa Constitució">
        Copa Constitució
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Andorran_Supercup" title="Andorran Supercup">
        Supercopa
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">
        futsal
       </a>
       . Andorra was admitted to
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">
        UEFA
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">
        FIFA
       </a>
       in the same year, 1996.
       <a href="/wiki/FC_Andorra" title="FC Andorra">
        FC Andorra
       </a>
       , a club based in
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
        Andorra la Vella
       </a>
       founded in 1942, compete in the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_football_league_system" title="Spanish football league system">
        Spanish football league system
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
        Rugby
       </a>
       is a traditional sport in Andorra, mainly influenced by the popularity in southern France. The
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_rugby_union_team" title="Andorra national rugby union team">
        Andorra national rugby union team
       </a>
       , nicknamed "
       <i>
        Els Isards
       </i>
       ", has impressed on the international stage in
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">
        rugby union
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_sevens" title="Rugby sevens">
        rugby sevens
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
        <a href="#cite_note-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/VPC_Andorra_XV" title="VPC Andorra XV">
        VPC Andorra XV
       </a>
       is a rugby team based in
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">
        Andorra la Vella
       </a>
       actually playing in the French championship.
      </p>
      <p>
       Basketball popularity has increased in the country since the 1990s, when the Andorran team
       <a href="/wiki/BC_Andorra" title="BC Andorra">
        BC Andorra
       </a>
       played in the top league of
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Liga_ACB" title="Liga ACB">
        Liga ACB
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After 18 years the club returned to the top league in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other sports practised in Andorra include
       <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">
        cycling
       </a>
       , volleyball,
       <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">
        judo
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Rules_football" title="Australian Rules football">
        Australian Rules football
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">
        handball
       </a>
       , swimming, gymnastics, tennis and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorsports" title="Motorsports">
        motorsports
       </a>
       . In 2012, Andorra raised its first national
       <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">
        cricket
       </a>
       team and played a home match against the Dutch Fellowship of Fairly Odd Places Cricket Club, the first match played in the history of Andorra at an altitude of 1,300 metres (4,300 ft).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Andorra first participated at the
       <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">
        Olympic Games
       </a>
       in 1976. The country has also appeared in every
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic" title="Winter Olympic">
        Winter Olympic
       </a>
       Games since 1976. Andorra competes in the
       <a href="/wiki/Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="Games of the Small States of Europe">
        Games of the Small States of Europe
       </a>
       being twice the host country in
       <a href="/wiki/1991_Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="1991 Games of the Small States of Europe">
        1991
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/2005_Games_of_the_Small_States_of_Europe" title="2005 Games of the Small States of Europe">
        2005
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As part of the Catalan cultural ambit, Andorra is home to a team of
       <a href="/wiki/Castell" title="Castell">
        castellers
       </a>
       , or Catalan human tower builders. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Castellers_d%27Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Castellers d'Andorra (page does not exist)">
        Castellers d'Andorra
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castellers_d%27Andorra" title="ca:Castellers d'Andorra">
         ca
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       , based in the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Coloma_d%27Andorra" title="Santa Coloma d'Andorra">
        Santa Coloma d'Andorra
       </a>
       , are recognized by the
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinadora_de_Colles_Castelleres_de_Catalunya" title="ca:Coordinadora de Colles Castelleres de Catalunya">
        Coordinadora de Colles Castelleres de Catalunya
       </a>
       , the governing body of castells.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_achievements">
        Major achievements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Major achievements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Ariadna_Tudel_Cuberes" title="Ariadna Tudel Cuberes">
        Ariadna Tudel Cuberes
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sophie_Dusautoir_Bertrand" title="Sophie Dusautoir Bertrand">
        Sophie Dusautoir Bertrand
       </a>
       earned the bronze medal in the women's team competition at the
       <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Championship_of_Ski_Mountaineering" title="2009 European Championship of Ski Mountaineering">
        2009 European Championship of Ski Mountaineering
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Joan_Verdu_Sanchez" title="Joan Verdu Sanchez">
        Joan Verdu Sanchez
       </a>
       earned a bronze medal in
       <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2012_Winter_Youth_Olympics" title="Alpine skiing at the 2012 Winter Youth Olympics">
        Alpine Skiing at the 2012 Winter Youth Olympics
       </a>
       . In 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Oliveras" title="Marc Oliveras">
        Marc Oliveras
       </a>
       earned a silver medal in
       <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing_at_the_2015_Winter_Universiade" title="Alpine skiing at the 2015 Winter Universiade">
        Alpine Skiing at the 2015 Winter Universiade
       </a>
       , while
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carmina_Pallas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carmina Pallas (page does not exist)">
        Carmina Pallas
       </a>
       earned a silver and a bronze medal in the same competition.
      </p>

                        <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">

              <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="text-align:left;">
               <div>
                <div class="plainlist">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <sup>
                    1
                   </sup>
                   <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">
                    Oceanic islands
                   </a>
                   within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <sup>
                    2
                   </sup>
                   Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.
                  </li>
                 </ul>
